Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Evidence required |\n| **Currently used?** | Referenced by running app, CI/CD, build? Cite specific references |\n| **Recommendation** | DELETE / CONSOLIDATE (with what) / MOVE / FLAG / KEEP — reason |\n\n## 6 Critical Differentiators\n\n1. **Compare, don't just catalog**: When similar files found, DIFF them. State \"X and Y are N% identical, differing in sections A, B\"\n2. **Group audit**: Audit similar files together. Compare all docker-compose files, all deploy scripts, all test configs within your batch\n3. **Mandatory duplication matrix**: Produce a matrix for your file group with overlap percentages (see format below)\n4. **Already-known issues**: You receive all findings from Passes 1-2. If you encounter a known issue, note \"Already tracked as issue #N\" and move on. DO NOT re-flag\n5. **Auto-KEEP for previously audited**: Do not re-audit files already deep-profiled in Pass 2. Focus on cross-cutting relationships only\n6. **Directory-level assessments**: For 50+ file directories, use strategic sampling (10-15 representative files) with directory-level summary\n\n## Mandatory Duplication Matrix\n\nProduce this for every group of similar files:\n\n```markdown\n## Duplication Matrix\n\n| File A | File B | Overlap % | Key Differences | Recommendation |\n|--------|--------|-----------|-----------------|----------------|\n```\n\n**Pass 3 is NOT complete without a duplication matrix** when similar files are detected.\n\n## Known-Issues Deduplication\n- Review the known issues list provided in your input\n- When encountering a previously flagged issue, note \"Already tracked as issue #N\"\n- Focus your effort on NEW cross-cutting findings\n\n## Output Format\nUse the batch-report template with 7-field profiles and duplication matrix.\n\n## Incremental Save Protocol\nSave after every 5-10 files. Never accumulate more than 10 unwritten results.\n","numLines":79,"startLine":1,"totalLines":79}}}

Detailed Design\n   211→\n   212→### 5.1 Data Models\n   213→\n   214→```python\n   215→# src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_gate.py\n   216→\n   217→from __future__ import annotations\n   218→\n   219→import ast\n   220→import re\n   221→from dataclasses import dataclass, field\n   222→from pathlib import Path\n   223→from typing import Literal\n   224→\n   225→from ..pipeline.models import GateCriteria, SemanticCheck\n   226→\n   227→\n   228→@dataclass\n   229→class WiringFinding:\n   230→    \"\"\"A single wiring verification finding.\"\"\"\n   231→\n   232→    finding_type: Literal[\"unwired_callable\", \"orphan_module\", \"unwired_registry\"]\n   233→    file_path: str\n   234→    symbol_name: str\n   235→    line_number: int\n   236→    detail: str\n   237→    severity: Literal[\"critical\", \"major\", \"info\"] = \"critical\"\n   238→```\n   239→\n   240→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-014 — info severity confirmed; Base already includes \"info\" in severity Literal -->\n   241→\n   242→```python\n   243→@dataclass\n   244→class WiringReport:\n   245→    \"\"\"Aggregate wiring analysis results.\n   246→\n   247→    Note on `clean` vs gate enforcement: The `clean` property returns True\n   248→    when analysis found zero issues. This represents analysis truth, not\n   249→    enforcement policy. Gate enforcement depends on rollout_mode -- see\n   250→    _zero_blocking_findings_for_mode(). Use blocking_for_mode() to determine\n   251→    whether findings would block under a given rollout mode.\n   252→    \"\"\"\n   253→\n   254→    target_dir: str\n   255→    files_analyzed: int = 0\n   256→    files_skipped: int = 0\n   257→    unwired_callables: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   258→    orphan_modules: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   259→    unwired_registries: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n   260→\n   261→    @property\n   262→    def total_findings(self) -> int:\n   263→        \"\"\"Single-source computation: category counts derive from list lengths.\"\"\"\n   264→        return (\n   265→            len(self.unwired_callables)\n   266→            + len(self.orphan_modules)\n   267→            + len(self.unwired_registries)\n   268→        )\n   269→\n   270→    @property\n   271→    def clean(self) -> bool:\n   272→        \"\"\"Returns True when analysis found zero issues.\n   273→\n   274→        This is analysis truth, not enforcement policy. Gate pass\n   275→        depends on rollout_mode via _zero_blocking_findings_for_mode().\n   276→        \"\"\"\n   277→        return self.total_findings == 0\n   278→\n   279→    def blocking_for_mode(self, mode: str) -> int:\n   280→        \"\"\"Return count of blocking findings for a given rollout mode.\n   281→\n   282→        - shadow: 0 (never blocks)\n   283→        - soft: critical_count only\n   284→        - full: critical_count + major_count\n   285→        \"\"\"\n   286→        all_findings = (\n   287→            self.unwired_callables + self.orphan_modules + self.unwired_registries\n   288→        )\n   289→        if mode == \"shadow\":\n   290→            return 0\n   291→        elif mode == \"soft\":\n   292→            return sum(1 for f in all_findings if f.severity == \"critical\")\n   293→        else:  # full\n   294→            return sum(\n   295→                1 for f in all_findings if f.severity in (\"critical\", \"major\")\n   296→            )\n   297→```\n   298→\n   299→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-008 — severity counts are derived properties from same finding lists -->\n   300→\n   301→**Single-source computation requirement**: Both category counts (`unwired_callable_count`, `orphan_module_count`, `unwired_registry_count`) and severity counts (`critical_count`, `major_count`, `info_count`) are computed by iterating the same typed finding lists. The `emit_report()` function derives both projections from `WiringReport`'s three lists, making the three-way invariant (`category_sum == severity_sum == total_findings`) a tautology. The semantic checks `_finding_counts_consistent` and `_severity_summary_consistent` validate the serialized form as a defense against report corruption or manual editing.\n   302→\n   303→<!-- Source: Debate X-006 / Refactor W-001 — renamed .passed to .clean, added blocking_for_mode() -->\n   304→<!-- Source: Debate A-008 consensus — added files_skipped field -->\n   305→\n   306→### 5.2 Analysis Functions\n   307→\n   308→#### 5.2.1 Unwired Callable Analysis\n   309→\n   310→**Purpose**: Detect constructor parameters typed `Optional[Callable]` (or `Callable | None`) with default `None` that are never explicitly provided at any call site.\n   311→\n   312→**Algorithm**:\n   313→\n   314→```\n   315→1. AST-parse all Python files in target directory\n   316→2. For each class __init__:\n   317→   a. Extract params where:\n   318→      - ast.unparse(annotation) matches \\bCallable\\b pattern\n   319→      - default is ast.Constant with value None\n   320→   b. Record: (class_name, param_name, file_path, line)\n   321→3. For each injectable:\n   322→   a. Search all Python files for call sites constructing that class\n   323→   b. Check if any call site provides the parameter by keyword\n   324→   c. Zero providers -> WiringFinding(unwired_callable)\n   325→```\n   326→\n   327→**Pattern matched** (from forensic report):\n   328→```python\n   329→class PortifyExecutor:\n   330→    def __init__(self, ..., step_runner: Optional[Callable] = None):\n   331→        ...\n   332→\n   333→# This call does NOT provide step_runner:\n   334→executor = PortifyExecutor(steps=steps, workdir=workdir, ...)\n   335→# -> Finding: unwired_callable, PortifyExecutor.step_runner\n   336→```\n   337→\n   338→**Whitelist**: `wiring_whitelist.yaml` with schema:\n   339→```yaml\n   340→unwired_callables:\n   341→  - symbol: \"module.path.ClassName.param_name\"\n   342→    reason: \"Intentional event hook\"\n   343→```\n   344→\n   345→Validation: entries missing `symbol` or `reason` are MALFORMED. In Phase 1 (shadow), malformed entries are logged as WARNING and skipped. In Phase 2+, malformed entries raise `WiringConfigError`.\n   346→\n   347→**Known limitation (v2.0)**: Import aliases and re-exports not resolved. Expected 30-70% FPR contribution. Planned fix in v2.1: alias pre-pass via `ast.Import`/`ast.ImportFrom` traversal with `__init__.py` chain resolution (max 3 hops).\n   348→\n   349→**Severity policy**:\n   350→- **critical**: execution/dispatch/enforcement behavior depends on the seam\n   351→- **major**: seam is dead but local fallback exists\n   352→- **info**: whitelisted intentional optional\n   353→\n   354→#### 5.2.2 Orphan Module Analysis\n   355→\n   356→**Purpose**: Detect Python files in provider directories whose exported functions are never imported by any consumer.\n   357→\n   358→**Algorithm**:\n   359→\n   360→```\n   361→1. Identify provider directories by convention:\n   362→   - names matching config.provider_dir_names\n   363→   - directories containing 3+ Python files with common function prefix\n   364→2. For each Python file in provider directory:\n   365→   a. AST-parse, extract top-level def (excluding _private)\n   366→   b. Search all Python files OUTSIDE provider dir for imports\n   367→   c. Zero importers -> WiringFinding(orphan_module)\n   368→```\n   369→\n   370→**Pattern matched**:\n   371→```python\n   372→# src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/steps/validate_config.py\n   373→def run_validate_config():  # never imported by executor.py\n   374→    ...\n   375→# -> Finding: orphan_module, steps/validate_config.py::run_validate_config\n   376→```\n   377→\n   378→**Exclusions**: `__init__.py`, `conftest.py`, `test_*.py`\n   379→\n   380→**Evidence rule**: A symbol is orphaned only if BOTH:\n   381→1. Direct analysis finds no effective import/call chain\n   382→2. Cleanup-audit evidence does not justify dynamic or deferred use\n   383→\n   384→#### 5.2.3 Unwired Registry Analysis\n   385→\n   386→**Purpose**: Detect dispatch registry dictionaries whose values reference non-importable functions.\n   387→\n   388→**Algorithm**:\n   389→\n   390→```\n   391→1. AST-parse all Python files\n   392→2. For each module-level assignment where:\n   393→   a. Target name matches REGISTRY_PATTERNS\n   394→   b. Value is a Dict literal\n   395→3. For each dict entry:\n   396→   a. If value is Name node: verify importable in scope\n   397→   b. If value is string: verify resolves to module.function\n   398→   c. If value is None: flag as explicit null handler\n   399→4. Unresolvable -> WiringFinding(unwired_registry)\n   400→```\n   401→\n   402→**Registry patterns** (configurable):\n   403→```python\n   404→DEFAULT_REGISTRY_PATTERNS = re.compile(\n   405→    r\"^(STEP_REGISTRY|STEP_DISPATCH|PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS|\"\n   406→    r\"\\w*_REGISTRY|\\w*_DISPATCH|\\w*_HANDLERS|\\w*_ROUTER|\\w*_BUILDERS)$\"\n   407→)\n   408→```\n   409→\n   410→Three detection classes:\n   411→1. **entry unresolved** -- mapped target does not resolve -> critical\n   412→2. **registry unused** -- registry or accessor has zero external consumers -> major\n   413→3. **explicit None** -- entry maps to None with no alternate handler -> major\n   414→\n   415→### 5.3 ToolOrchestrator AST Analyzer Plugin\n   416→\n   417→```python\n   418→# src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_analyzer.py\n   419→\n   420→from __future__ import annotations\n   421→\n   422→import ast\n   423→from pathlib import Path\n   424→\n   425→from .tool_orchestrator import FileAnalysis\n   426→\n   427→\n   428→def ast_analyze_file(file_path: Path, content: str) -> FileAnalysis:\n   429→    \"\"\"AST-based file analyzer for ToolOrchestrator injection.\n   430→\n   431→    Populates the `references` field that the default line-based\n   432→    analyzer leaves empty.\n   433→\n   434→    Usage: ToolOrchestrator(analyzer=ast_analyze_file)\n   435→    \"\"\"\n   436→    try:\n   437→        tree = ast.parse(content, filename=str(file_path))\n   438→    except SyntaxError:\n   439→        return FileAnalysis(\n   440→            imports=[], exports=[], references=[], metadata={}\n   441→        )\n   442→\n   443→    imports = _extract_imports(tree)\n   444→    exports = _extract_exports(tree)\n   445→    references = _extract_references(tree, file_path)\n   446→\n   447→    return FileAnalysis(\n   448→        imports=imports,\n   449→        exports=exports,\n   450→        references=references,\n   451→        metadata={\n   452→            \"has_dispatch_registry\": _has_registry(tree),\n   453→            \"injectable_callables\": _count_injectable_callables(tree),\n   454→        },\n   455→    )\n   456→```\n   457→\n   458→**Integration**: Pass as `analyzer` parameter to `ToolOrchestrator.__init__()`. This populates the empty `references` field, improving:\n   459→- `dependency_graph.py` Tier-A edges (actual imports vs line-based)\n   460→- `dead_code.py` detection (symbol-level vs file-level)\n   461→- `profile_generator.py` coupling metric (real deps vs stem-matching)\n   462→\n   463→<!-- Source: Debate risk #2 / Refactor W-002 — ToolOrchestrator cut criteria -->\n   464→#### 5.3.1 Cut Criteria\n   465→\n   466→If T06 (ToolOrchestrator AST plugin) is not complete by the time T08 (roadmap integration) begins, defer T06 to v2.1. Core wiring gate functionality (T01-T05, T07-T10) does not depend on the ToolOrchestrator plugin. The cleanup-audit integration (Mode C) operates with reduced accuracy but still functions using line-based analysis.\n   467→\n   468→### 5.4 Report Format\n   469→\n   470→YAML frontmatter + Markdown body, conforming to `GateCriteria` validation:\n   471→\n   472→```yaml\n   473→---\n   474→gate: wiring-verification\n   475→target_dir: src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify\n   476→files_analyzed: 14\n   477→files_skipped: 0\n   478→rollout_mode: shadow\n   479→analysis_complete: true\n   480→audit_artifacts_used: 0\n   481→unwired_callable_count: 1\n   482→orphan_module_count: 2\n   483→unwired_registry_count: 0\n   484→critical_count: 3\n   485→major_count: 0\n   486→info_count: 0\n   487→total_findings: 3\n   488→blocking_findings: 3\n   489→whitelist_entries_applied: 0\n   490→---\n   491→```\n   492→\n   493→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-014 — flat frontmatter confirmed, no nested severity_summary block -->\n   494→\n   495→**Serialization**: All string-valued frontmatter fields MUST use `yaml.safe_dump()` to prevent YAML injection. Integer/boolean gate-evaluated fields are exempt.\n   496→\n   497→**Whitelist visibility**: `whitelist_entries_applied` is ALWAYS present. Zero if no whitelist configured.\n   498→\n   499→<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 7.3 — required report body sections (S-002) -->\n   500→#### 5.4.1 Required Body Sections\n   501→\n   502→The Markdown body of the wiring verification report MUST contain these 7 sections in order:\n   503→\n   504→1. **Summary** -- overall finding counts, scope analyzed, rollout mode\n   505→2. **Unwired Optional Callable Injections** -- per-finding detail for `unwired_callable` type\n   506→3. **Orphan Modules / Symbols** -- per-finding detail for `orphan_module` type\n   507→4. **Unregistered Dispatch Entries** -- per-finding detail for `unwired_registry` type\n   508→5. **Suppressions and Dynamic Retention** -- whitelist entries applied, audit evidence used\n   509→6. **Recommended Remediation** -- actionable fix guidance per finding category\n   510→7. **Evidence and Limitations** -- known FPR sources, alias limitations, analysis boundaries\n   511→\n   512→This ensures human-readable reports have consistent structure across runs and are useful for both automated gate validation and manual review.\n   513→\n   514→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-001 / Refactor W-004 — _extract_frontmatter_values() helper -->\n   515→### 5.5 Frontmatter Value Extraction\n   516→\n   517→All semantic check functions share a private helper:\n   518→\n   519→```python\n   520→def _extract_frontmatter_values(content: str) -> dict[str, str]:\n   521→    \"\"\"Extract frontmatter key-value pairs from report content.\n   522→\n   523→    Uses the _FRONTMATTER_RE regex pattern (duplicated from\n   524→    pipeline/gates.py:77 as a private constant to preserve\n   525→    NFR-007 layering) to extract frontmatter key-value pairs.\n   526→\n   527→    Returns a dict mapping each key to its raw string value.\n   528→    Each semantic check calls this helper once and casts values\n   529→    as needed (int(), string comparison).\n   530→    \"\"\"\n   531→```\n   532→\n   533→This helper lives in `audit/wiring_gate.py`, not in `pipeline/*`, preserving the layering constraint (NFR-007). Estimated: ~15 LOC.\n   534→\n   535→**Why not modify `_check_frontmatter()`**: That function is in `pipeline/gates.py` which must remain domain-agnostic. Adding a value-extraction return type would change its contract, violating the \"zero changes to pipeline/*\" constraint.\n   536→\n   537→### 5.6 Gate Definition\n   538→\n   539→```python\n   540→WIRING_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   541→    required_frontmatter_fields=[\n   542→        \"gate\",\n   543→        \"target_dir\",\n   544→        \"files_analyzed\",\n   545→        \"rollout_mode\",\n   546→        \"analysis_complete\",\n   547→        \"unwired_callable_count\",\n   548→        \"orphan_module_count\",\n   549→        \"unwired_registry_count\",\n   550→        \"critical_count\",\n   551→        \"major_count\",\n   552→        \"info_count\",\n   553→        \"total_findings\",\n   554→        \"blocking_findings\",\n   555→        \"whitelist_entries_applied\",\n   556→        \"files_skipped\",\n   557→        \"audit_artifacts_used\",\n   558→    ],\n   559→    min_lines=10,\n   560→    enforcement_tier=\"STRICT\",\n   561→    semantic_checks=[\n   562→        SemanticCheck(\n   563→            name=\"analysis_complete_true\",\n   564→            check_fn=_analysis_complete_true,\n   565→            failure_message=\"analysis_complete must be true\",\n   566→        ),\n   567→        SemanticCheck(\n   568→            name=\"recognized_rollout_mode\",\n   569→            check_fn=_recognized_rollout_mode,\n   570→            failure_message=\"rollout_mode must be shadow, soft, or full\",\n   571→        ),\n   572→        SemanticCheck(\n   573→            name=\"finding_counts_consistent\",\n   574→            check_fn=_finding_counts_consistent,\n   575→            failure_message=(\n   576→                \"total_findings must equal \"\n   577→                \"unwired_callable_count + orphan_module_count + unwired_registry_count\"\n   578→            ),\n   579→        ),\n   580→        SemanticCheck(\n   581→            name=\"severity_summary_consistent\",\n   582→            check_fn=_severity_summary_consistent,\n   583→            failure_message=(\n   584→                \"critical_count + major_count + info_count must equal total_findings\"\n   585→            ),\n   586→        ),\n   587→        SemanticCheck(\n   588→            name=\"zero_blocking_findings_for_mode\",\n   589→            check_fn=_zero_blocking_findings_for_mode,\n   590→            failure_message=\"blocking_findings must be 0 for gate pass at current rollout_mode\",\n   591→        ),\n   592→    ],\n   593→)\n   594→```\n   595→\n   596→**Mode-aware enforcement** (key design decision):\n   597→\n   598→The `_zero_blocking_findings_for_mode` check reads `rollout_mode` and `blocking_findings` from frontmatter:\n   599→- **shadow**: always returns `True` (findings logged, never block)\n   600→- **soft**: returns `True` if `blocking_findings == 0` (only critical block)\n   601→- **full**: returns `True` if `blocking_findings == 0` (all findings block)\n   602→\n   603→The `blocking_findings` field is computed by the emitter based on rollout mode:\n   604→- shadow: `blocking_findings = 0` always\n   605→- soft: `blocking_findings = critical_count`\n   606→- full: `blocking_findings = critical_count + major_count`\n   607→\n   608→This encodes rollout policy into the report artifact, keeping semantic checks as pure content validators per the `SemanticCheck` contract.\n   609→\n   610→### 5.7 Roadmap Pipeline Integration\n   611→\n   612→**5-step process** (per gate-system-deep-analysis Section 8):\n   613→\n   614→**Step 1**: Define `WIRING_GATE` in `audit/wiring_gate.py`\n   615→\n   616→**Step 2**: Define prompt in `roadmap/prompts.py`:\n   617→```python\n   618→def build_wiring_verification_prompt(merge_file: Path, spec_source: str) -> str:\n   619→    \"\"\"Prompt for wiring-verification step (deterministic, not LLM).\"\"\"\n   620→    return \"\"  # Non-LLM step; prompt unused but required by Step contract\n   621→```\n   622→\n   623→**Step 3**: Import into `roadmap/executor.py`\n   624→\n   625→**Step 4**: Add to `_build_steps()` after `spec-fidelity` (line 473):\n   626→```python\n   627→Step(\n   628→    id=\"wiring-verification\",\n   629→    prompt=build_wiring_verification_prompt(merge_file, spec_source),\n   630→    output_file=out / \"wiring-verification.md\",\n   631→    gate=WIRING_GATE,\n   632→    timeout_seconds=60,\n   633→    inputs=[merge_file, spec_fidelity_file],\n   634→    retry_limit=0,                         # Deterministic; retry won't help\n   635→    gate_mode=GateMode.TRAILING,           # Shadow: non-blocking\n   636→),\n   637→```\n   638→\n   639→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-012 — retry_limit=0 semantics documented -->\n   640→**`retry_limit=0` semantics**: Per `pipeline/executor.py:158`, `max_attempts = retry_limit + 1`. So `retry_limit=0` means the step executes exactly once with no retries. This is correct for a deterministic step where re-execution produces identical results. The only retry-worthy scenario (transient filesystem errors) should be handled within the analysis function itself.\n   641→\n   642→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-003 — explicit _get_all_step_ids() synchronization requirement -->\n   643→**Step 5**: Update `_get_all_step_ids()` (line 538) and `ALL_GATES` (line 933).\n   644→\n   645→`_get_all_step_ids()` MUST be updated to include `\"wiring-verification\"` after `\"spec-fidelity\"` and before `\"remediate\"`. The existing desynchronization between `_build_steps()` (8 steps) and `_get_all_step_ids()` (11 IDs including `remediate` and `certify`) is intentional -- `remediate` and `certify` are conditionally executed steps. `wiring-verification` belongs in the unconditional pipeline, so it goes in both functions.\n   646→\n   647→<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 5.3 — why _build_steps() is the correct insertion point (S-001) -->\n   648→#### 5.7.1 Why `_build_steps()` Is the Correct Insertion Point\n   649→\n   650→The codebase has no dynamic gate registry for roadmap execution. Gates are wired statically at `Step` construction time. The integration point is not an external registry; it is a new `Step(...)` entry in `_build_steps()`.\n   651→\n   652→The repository already contains a design precedent for a post-merge deterministic step: the anti-instinct audit step is modeled as a normal `Step` in `_build_steps()` but handled specially by the executor as a non-LLM operation. That is the correct pattern for wiring verification as well.\n   653→\n   654→**Executor special-casing**: In `roadmap_run_step()`, detect `step.id == \"wiring-verification\"`:\n   655→```python\n   656→if step.id == \"wiring-verification\":\n   657→    report = run_wiring_analysis(target_dir=config.source_dir)\n   658→    emit_report(report, step.output_file, enforcement_mode=config.wiring_rollout_mode)\n   659→    return StepResult(step=step, status=StepStatus.PASS)\n   660→```\n   661→\n   662→**Shadow**: `GateMode.TRAILING` uses `TrailingGateRunner` for async non-blocking evaluation. Failures persist to `DeferredRemediationLog`.\n   663→\n   664→**Full**: Switch to `GateMode.BLOCKING`. `resolve_gate_mode()` forces release scope to BLOCKING regardless.\n   665→\n   666→<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 9.3 — resume behavior (S-003) -->\n   667→#### 5.7.2 Resume Behavior\n   668→\n   669→Because the roadmap pipeline already resumes by gate-passing existing artifacts, the new wiring-verification step naturally fits current resume behavior if:\n   670→\n   671→1. `wiring-verification.md` is deterministic (same inputs produce same output)\n   672→2. Its gate result is reproducible (semantic checks are pure functions over content)\n   673→3. `_get_all_step_ids()` is updated to include `wiring-verification`\n   674→\n   675→No special resume handling is required. The existing resume mechanism detects the output file, evaluates the gate, and skips the step if the gate passes.\n   676→\n   677→### 5.8 Sprint Integration\n   678→\n   679→```python\n   680→# sprint/models.py\n   681→wiring_gate_mode: Literal[\"off\", \"shadow\", \"soft\", \"full\"] = \"shadow\"\n   682→\n   683→# sprint/executor.py -- after task classification\n   684→if config.wiring_gate_mode != \"off\":\n   685→    wiring_report_path = work_dir / f\"{task_id}-wiring-report.md\"\n   686→    report = run_wiring_analysis(target_dir=config.source_dir)\n   687→    emit_report(report, wiring_report_path,\n   688→                enforcement_mode=config.wiring_gate_mode)\n   689→\n   690→    if config.wiring_gate_mode == \"shadow\":\n   691→        logger.info(f\"[shadow] Wiring gate: {report.total_findings} findings\")\n   692→    elif config.wiring_gate_mode == \"soft\":\n   693→        if not report.clean:\n   694→            tui.warn(f\"Wiring gate: {report.total_findings} findings\")\n   695→    elif config.wiring_gate_mode == \"full\":\n   696→        passed, reason = gate_passed(wiring_report_path, WIRING_GATE)\n   697→        if not passed:\n   698→            ...  # Trigger SprintGatePolicy.build_remediation_step()\n   699→```\n   700→\n   701→---\n   702→\n   703→<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n   704→## 6. Cleanup-Audit Agent Integration\n   705→\n   706→### 6.1 Agent Extension Summary\n   707→\n   708→All 5 agents are behavioral specs (`.md` files in `src/superclaude/agents/`). Extensions are additive -- no tools change, no existing rules removed.\n   709→\n   710→| Agent | Tools | Change |\n   711→|-------|-------|--------|\n   712→| audit-scanner (Haiku) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add `REVIEW:wiring` classification signal |\n   713→| audit-analyzer (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add 9th mandatory field: \"Wiring path\" |\n   714→| audit-comparator (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add cross-file wiring consistency check |\n   715→| audit-validator (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add Check 5: Wiring Claim Verification |\n   716→| audit-consolidator (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob, Write | Add \"Wiring Health\" section to report |\n   717→\n   718→### 6.2 audit-scanner: REVIEW:wiring Signal\n   719→\n   720→For Python source files, check:\n   721→- File contains `Optional[Callable]` parameter with `= None` default\n   722→- File defines module-level dict matching `*_REGISTRY`, `*_DISPATCH`, `*_HANDLERS`\n   723→- File is in a provider directory (`steps/`, `handlers/`, `validators/`, `checks/`)\n   724→\n   725→Files with wiring indicators get `REVIEW:wiring`, proceeding to Pass 2 even if otherwise `KEEP`.\n   726→\n   727→### 6.3 audit-analyzer: 9th Mandatory Field\n   728→\n   729→For `REVIEW:wiring` files, add:\n   730→\n   731→| Field | Description |\n   732→|-------|-------------|\n   733→| Wiring path | Declaration -> Registration -> Invocation chain. Each link stated or \"MISSING\" |\n   734→\n   735→New finding types:\n   736→- `UNWIRED_DECLARATION` -- symbol declared but never registered/invoked\n   737→- `BROKEN_REGISTRATION` -- registry entry references non-importable function\n   738→\n   739→### 6.4 audit-validator: Check 5\n   740→\n   741→**Wiring Claim Verification**:\n   742→1. Verify declared callable parameters against call site arguments\n   743→2. Verify registry entries resolve to importable symbols\n   744→3. Verify \"Wiring path\" field chain is complete\n   745→\n   746→**Critical fail**: DELETE recommendation on a file with a live wiring path.\n   747→\n   748→### 6.5 ToolOrchestrator Integration\n   749→\n   750→```python\n   751→orchestrator = ToolOrchestrator(analyzer=ast_analyze_file)\n   752→```\n   753→\n   754→Populates `FileAnalysis.references`, improving `dependency_graph.py`, `dead_code.py`, `profile_generator.py`.\n   755→\n   756→### 6.6 Authority Rule\n   757→\n   758→**Hybrid mode**: Direct deterministic analysis is authoritative. Cleanup-audit evidence acts as false-positive suppressor. Correctness does not depend on prior audit runs.\n   759→\n   760→---\n   761→\n   762→<!-- Source: Base (original), with incorporations from Variant C (S-005, FPR calibration) and Invariant INV-006 (W-003, grace_period) -->\n   763→## 7. Rollout Plan\n   764→\n   765→### Phase 1: Shadow (this release)\n   766→\n   767→**Pre-activation checklist** (blocking):\n   768→1. Confirm `provider_dir_names` matches at least one real directory\n   769→2. First-run zero-findings sanity check (>50 files must produce >0 findings)\n   770→\n   771→**Behavior**: Roadmap `GateMode.TRAILING` + Sprint `shadow` + Cleanup-audit `REVIEW:wiring`\n   772→\n   773→<!-- Source: Invariant INV-006 / Refactor W-003 — grace_period interaction note -->\n   774→**Operational note on `grace_period` interaction**: Roadmap configurations should set `grace_period > 0` during shadow rollout to enable `GateMode.TRAILING` behavior via `TrailingGateRunner`. If `grace_period = 0` forces BLOCKING (per `pipeline/executor.py:160-163`), shadow mode still passes because `_zero_blocking_findings_for_mode` reads `rollout_mode=shadow` from frontmatter and returns True unconditionally, and the emitter sets `blocking_findings=0` in shadow mode. However, TRAILING mode provides cleaner operational semantics (deferred evaluation rather than immediate pass-through).\n   775→\n   776→### Phase 2: Soft (release +1)\n   777→\n   778→**Criteria**: FPR < 15%, TPR > 50%, p95 < 5s\n   779→\n   780→<!-- Source: Variant C, Section 9 Phase 2 — FPR calibration formula (S-005) -->\n   781→**FPR calibration**: Set thresholds at `measured_FPR + 2 sigma` above re-export noise floor. Phase 2 MUST NOT activate if unwired-callable FPR cannot be separated from noise. This statistical approach prevents premature soft-mode activation when FPR variance is high.\n   782→\n   783→**Behavior**: `rollout_mode=soft`, `blocking_findings = critical_count`\n   784→\n   785→### Phase 3: Full (release +2)\n   786→\n   787→**Criteria**: FPR < 5%, TPR > 80%, whitelist stable 5+ sprints\n   788→\n   789→**Behavior**: `GateMode.BLOCKING`, `rollout_mode=full`, `blocking_findings = critical + major`\n   790→\n   791→---\n   792→\n   793→<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n   794→## 8. Interface Contracts\n   795→\n   796→### 8.1 Public API\n   797→\n   798→```python\n   799→def run_wiring_analysis(target_dir: Path, config: WiringConfig | None = None) -> WiringReport\n   800→def emit_report(report: WiringReport, output_path: Path, enforcement_mode: str = \"shadow\") -> None\n   801→def ast_analyze_file(file_path: Path, content: str) -> FileAnalysis\n   802→```\n   803→\n   804→### 8.2 Gate Contract\n   805→\n   806→| Frontmatter Field | Type | Pass Condition |\n   807→|-------------------|------|----------------|\n   808→| `gate` | string | `\"wiring-verification\"` |\n   809→| `target_dir` | string | Non-empty |\n   810→| `files_analyzed` | int | >= 0 |\n   811→| `files_skipped` | int | >= 0 |\n   812→| `rollout_mode` | string | `shadow` / `soft` / `full` |\n   813→| `analysis_complete` | bool | `true` |\n   814→| `unwired_callable_count` | int | Present |\n   815→| `orphan_module_count` | int | Present |\n   816→| `unwired_registry_count` | int | Present |\n   817→| `critical_count` | int | Present |\n   818→| `major_count` | int | Present |\n   819→| `info_count` | int | Present |\n   820→| `total_findings` | int | = sum of type counts |\n   821→| `blocking_findings` | int | Must be 0 |\n   822→| `whitelist_entries_applied` | int | >= 0 |\n   823→\n   824→### 8.3 Dependency Direction\n   825→\n   826→```\n   827→audit/wiring_gate.py    --> pipeline/models.py     (GateCriteria, SemanticCheck)\n   828→audit/wiring_analyzer.py --> audit/tool_orchestrator.py (FileAnalysis)\n   829→audit/wiring_config.py  --> (stdlib only)\n   830→roadmap/executor.py     --> audit/wiring_gate.py\n   831→sprint/executor.py      --> audit/wiring_gate.py\n   832→pipeline/*              --> NOTHING from audit/roadmap/sprint\n   833→```\n   834→\n   835→---\n   836→\n   837→<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n   838→## 9. Decisions\n   961→\n   962→| # | Decision | Rationale |\n   963→|---|----------|-----------|\n   964→| D1 | Enforcement is artifact-based | Fits SemanticCheck contract: `check_fn(content: str) -> bool` validates report content, not repository state |\n   965→| D2 | Deterministic Python, not LLM | Wiring needs precision; LLM synthesis rejected as \"too weak for wiring assurance and too dependent on narrative interpretation\" (see D2a below) |\n   966→| D3 | Extend audit-analyzer, no new agent | Reuse 8-field profile; single \"Wiring path\" chain field forces full chain tracing |\n   967→| D4 | Insert via _build_steps() after spec-fidelity | Static wiring pattern; no dynamic gate registry exists (see Section 5.7.1) |\n   968→| D5 | Shadow/soft/full via rollout_mode frontmatter | No parallel infra; policy encoded in artifact, checks remain pure content validators |\n   969→| D6 | GateMode.TRAILING for shadow phase | Existing TrailingGateRunner; mode-aware checks as safeguard if BLOCKING forced |\n   970→| D7 | AST analyzer as ToolOrchestrator plugin | Reuses existing seam; parallel track with explicit cut criteria |\n   971→\n   972→<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 9.1 — rejected option documentation (S-008) -->\n   973→### D2a: Rejected Alternative -- LLM Report Generation\n   974→\n   975→**Rejected**: LLM-only report generation from pre-read analyses.\n   976→\n   977→**Reason**: Too weak for wiring assurance and too dependent on narrative interpretation. Wiring verification requires deterministic precision (exact symbol resolution, exact import chain tracing) that LLM synthesis cannot reliably provide. LLM-generated reports would introduce non-reproducibility and make gate results unreliable across runs.\n   978→\n   979→**Chosen approach**: Executor-special-cased deterministic step that gathers source scope, loads optional cleanup-audit artifacts, runs deterministic wiring analysis, emits the report, and validates via `gate_passed()`.\n   980→\n   981→---\n   982→\n   983→<!-- Source: Variant C, Section 18 — coordination notes (S-004) -->\n   984→## 15. Problem Statement\n\nThe pipeline's gate infrastructure validates **documents, not code integration**. Components defined in specifications and decomposed into tasks can pass every existing gate while producing code where modules are never connected to their consumers.\n\n**Evidence**: 32 unwired symbols across 14 files in 5 subsystems (from `cli-unwired-components-audit.md`):\n\n| System | Pattern | Count |\n|--------|---------|-------|\n| cli-portify executor | `Optional[Callable]=None` defaults never provided | 11 |\n| cli-portify gates | `GATE_REGISTRY` + `gate_*()` with zero callers | 12 |\n| sprint executor | `SprintGatePolicy` defined, never instantiated | 4 |\n| audit modules | `evidence_gate()`, `manifest_gate()` zero callers | 4 |\n| roadmap gates | `DEVIATION_ANALYSIS_GATE` defined, never wired to Step | 1 |\n\n### What changed from v1.0\n\nv1.0 was authored before the Phase 1 deep analysis. This v2.0 spec:\n\n- Adds precise substrate references with exact line numbers\n- Adds cleanup-audit agent integration (v1.0 covered sprint only)\n- Adds dual-mode operation: roadmap pipeline gate + cleanup-audit pass extension\n- Adds `ToolOrchestrator` analyzer plugin for audit infrastructure reuse\n- Adds `GateMode.TRAILING` integration via `TrailingGateRunner` for shadow phase\n- Adds explicit design constraint: deterministic Python analysis, not LLM synthesis\n- Refines rollout plan with `resolve_gate_mode()` scope awareness\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n## 2. Goals and Non-Goals\n\n### Goals\n\n| # | Goal | Verification |\n|---|------|-------------|\n| G-001 | Detect unwired injectable dependencies (`Optional[Callable]=None` never provided) | SC-001 |\n| G-002 | Detect orphan modules (exported functions never imported by any consumer) | SC-002 |\n| G-003 | Detect unwired dispatch registries (entries mapping to non-importable functions) | SC-003 |\n| G-004 | Emit structured YAML+Markdown report compatible with `GateCriteria`/`SemanticCheck` | SC-004 |\n| G-005 | Deploy in shadow mode initially, path to soft and full enforcement | SC-006 |\n| G-006 | Plug into roadmap pipeline via `_build_steps()` as post-merge step | SC-005 |\n| G-007 | Integrate with cleanup-audit protocol (extend audit-scanner, audit-analyzer, audit-validator) | SC-011, SC-012 |\n| G-008 | Reuse `ToolOrchestrator` analyzer injection seam for AST analysis | SC-013 |\n\n### Non-Goals (v2.0)\n\n- No-op fallback detection (deferred to v2.1 pending shadow data)\n- Cross-language analysis (Python only)\n- Runtime behavioral verification (Smoke Test Gate domain)\n- Dynamic dispatch resolution (`**kwargs`, `getattr`, `importlib`)\n- Modifying `SemanticCheck` interface: `check_fn: Callable[[str], bool]` preserved\n- Modifying `gate_passed()` in `pipeline/gates.py`\n- Creating parallel gate infrastructure\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n## 3. Design Constraints\n\n### 3.1 Preserve the existing gate substrate\n\nThis release is a **consumer** of:\n\n| Symbol | Location | Contract |\n|--------|----------|----------|\n| `SemanticCheck` | `pipeline/models.py:58-65` | `check_fn: Callable[[str], bool]` -- pure, no I/O |\n| `GateCriteria` | `pipeline/models.py:67-75` | `required_frontmatter_fields`, `min_lines`, `enforcement_tier`, `semantic_checks` |\n| `Step` | `pipeline/models.py:77-90` | `gate: GateCriteria`, `gate_mode: GateMode` |\n| `GateMode` | `pipeline/models.py:46-55` | `BLOCKING`, `TRAILING` |\n| `gate_passed()` | `pipeline/gates.py:20-74` | `(Path, GateCriteria) -> tuple[bool, str \\| None]` |\n| `TrailingGateRunner` | `pipeline/trailing_gate.py:88-213` | `.submit(step, gate_check)` for non-blocking evaluation |\n| `DeferredRemediationLog` | `pipeline/trailing_gate.py:489-578` | Persistence for shadow/soft mode failures |\n\n**No signature changes** to any of these.\n\n### 3.2 Preserve layering (NFR-007)\n\n```\naudit/*       --may import--> pipeline/models.py\nroadmap/*     --may import--> audit/*, pipeline/*\nsprint/*      --may import--> audit/*, pipeline/*\npipeline/*    --MUST NOT import--> roadmap/*, audit/*, sprint/*\n```\n\n### 3.3 Separate analysis from enforcement\n\nThree distinct layers, matching existing document-first gate architecture:\n\n1. **Deterministic wiring analysis** -- pure Python over source files (no LLM)\n2. **Artifact emission** -- Markdown report with YAML frontmatter\n3. **Gate enforcement** -- `gate_passed(report_file, WIRING_GATE)` via existing substrate\n\n### 3.4 Extend, don't duplicate cleanup-audit\n\n- Extend `audit-analyzer` evidence collection, not create new agent types\n- Reuse existing audit structural outputs as advisory inputs\n- Keep the roadmap wiring step authoritative through direct deterministic analysis\n- Use audit evidence as false-positive suppressor, not primary data source\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n## 4. Architecture\n\n### 4.1 System Context\n\n```\nEXISTING SUBSTRATE (zero changes)              NEW COMPONENTS\n================================              ==============\n\npipeline/models.py:58-75 Dataclass\n\nThe `audit/wiring_config.py` module contains the concrete configuration model:\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass WiringConfig:\n    registry_patterns: re.Pattern = DEFAULT_REGISTRY_PATTERNS\n    provider_dir_names: frozenset[str] = frozenset({\n        \"steps\", \"handlers\", \"validators\", \"checks\",\n    })\n    whitelist_path: Path | None = None\n    exclude_patterns: list[str] = field(default_factory=lambda: [\n        \"test_*.py\", \"conftest.py\", \"__init__.py\",\n    ])\n```\n\n### 4.3 Dual-Mode Operation\n\n#### Mode A: Roadmap Pipeline Gate (post-merge deterministic step)\n\nAppends to the post-merge validation chain:\n\n```\nStep 6: merge           -> MERGE_GATE               (existing)\nStep 7: test-strategy   -> TEST_STRATEGY_GATE        (existing)\nStep 8: spec-fidelity   -> SPEC_FIDELITY_GATE        (existing)\nStep 9: wiring-verify   -> WIRING_GATE               <- NEW\n```\n\n**Insertion point**: `roadmap/executor.py:_build_steps()`, after `spec-fidelity` (line 473).\n\n**Critical design choice**: This is a **deterministic Python step**, not an LLM step. The executor special-cases it: runs `run_wiring_analysis()`, emits `wiring-verification.md`, then normal gate validation applies.\n\n#### Mode B: Sprint Post-Task Check\n\nRuns `run_wiring_analysis()` after each task completes in the sprint loop.\n\n**Integration point**: `sprint/executor.py`, after task classification, before status finalization.\n\n#### Mode C: Cleanup-Audit Pass Extension\n\nExtends existing 3-pass audit with wiring-aware capabilities via agent behavioral rule additions (see Section 6).\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n## 5. Detailed Design\n\n### 5.1 Data Models\n\n```python\n# src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_gate.py\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport ast\nimport re\nfrom dataclasses import dataclass, field\nfrom pathlib import Path\nfrom typing import Literal\n\nfrom ..pipeline.models import GateCriteria, SemanticCheck\n\n\n@dataclass\nclass WiringFinding:\n    \"\"\"A single wiring verification finding.\"\"\"\n\n    finding_type: Literal[\"unwired_callable\", \"orphan_module\", \"unwired_registry\"]\n    file_path: str\n    symbol_name: str\n    line_number: int\n    detail: str\n    severity: Literal[\"critical\", \"major\", \"info\"] = \"critical\"\n```\n\n<!-- Source: Invariant INV-014 — info severity confirmed; Base already includes \"info\" in severity Literal -->\n\n```python\n@dataclass\nclass WiringReport:\n    \"\"\"Aggregate wiring analysis results.\n\n    Note on `clean` vs gate enforcement: The `clean` property returns True\n    when analysis found zero issues. This represents analysis truth, not\n    enforcement policy. Gate enforcement depends on rollout_mode -- see\n    _zero_blocking_findings_for_mode(). Use blocking_for_mode() to determine\n    whether findings would block under a given rollout mode.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    target_dir: str\n    files_analyzed: int = 0\n    files_skipped: int = 0\n    unwired_callables: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n    orphan_modules: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n    unwired_registries: list[WiringFinding] = field(default_factory=list)\n\n    @property\n    def total_findings(self) -> int:\n        \"\"\"Single-source computation: category counts derive from list lengths.\"\"\"\n        return (\n            len(self.unwired_callables)\n            + len(self.orphan_modules)\n            + len(self.unwired_registries)\n        )\n\n    @property\n    def clean(self) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"Returns True when analysis found zero issues.\n\n        This is analysis truth, not enforcement policy. Gate pass\n        depends on rollout_mode via _zero_blocking_findings_for_mode().\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.total_findings == 0\n\n    def blocking_for_mode(self, mode: str) -> int:\n        \"\"\"Return count of blocking findings for a given rollout mode.\n\n        - shadow: 0 (never blocks)\n        - soft: critical_count only\n        - full: critical_count + major_count\n        \"\"\"\n        all_findings = (\n            self.unwired_callables + self.orphan_modules + self.unwired_registries\n        )\n        if mode == \"shadow\":\n            return 0\n        elif mode == \"soft\":\n            return sum(1 for f in all_findings if f.severity == \"critical\")\n        else:  # full\n            return sum(\n                1 for f in all_findings if f.severity in (\"critical\", \"major\")\n            )\n```\n\n<!-- Source: Invariant INV-008 — severity counts are derived properties from same finding lists -->\n\n**Single-source computation requirement**: Both category counts (`unwired_callable_count`, `orphan_module_count`, `unwired_registry_count`) and severity counts (`critical_count`, `major_count`, `info_count`) are computed by iterating the same typed finding lists. The `emit_report()` function derives both projections from `WiringReport`'s three lists, making the three-way invariant (`category_sum == severity_sum == total_findings`) a tautology. The semantic checks `_finding_counts_consistent` and `_severity_summary_consistent` validate the serialized form as a defense against report corruption or manual editing.\n\n<!-- Source: Debate X-006 / Refactor W-001 — renamed .passed to .clean, added blocking_for_mode() -->\n<!-- Source: Debate A-008 consensus — added files_skipped field -->\n\n### 5.2 Analysis Functions\n\n#### 5.2.1 Unwired Callable Analysis\n\n**Purpose**: Detect constructor parameters typed `Optional[Callable]` (or `Callable | None`) with default `None` that are never explicitly provided at any call site.\n\n**Algorithm**:\n\n```\n1. AST-parse all Python files in target directory\n2. For each class __init__:\n   a. Extract params where:\n      - ast.unparse(annotation) matches \\bCallable\\b pattern\n      - default is ast.Constant with value None\n   b. Record: (class_name, param_name, file_path, line)\n3. For each injectable:\n   a. Search all Python files for call sites constructing that class\n   b. Check if any call site provides the parameter by keyword\n   c. Zero providers -> WiringFinding(unwired_callable)\n```\n\n**Pattern matched** (from forensic report):\n```python\nclass PortifyExecutor:\n    def __init__(self, ..., step_runner: Optional[Callable] = None):\n        ...\n\n# This call does NOT provide step_runner:\nexecutor = PortifyExecutor(steps=steps, workdir=workdir, ...)\n# -> Finding: unwired_callable, PortifyExecutor.step_runner\n```\n\n**Whitelist**: `wiring_whitelist.yaml` with schema:\n```yaml\nunwired_callables:\n  - symbol: \"module.path.ClassName.param_name\"\n    reason: \"Intentional event hook\"\n```\n\nValidation: entries missing `symbol` or `reason` are MALFORMED. In Phase 1 (shadow), malformed entries are logged as WARNING and skipped. In Phase 2+, malformed entries raise `WiringConfigError`.\n\n**Known limitation (v2.0)**: Import aliases and re-exports not resolved. Expected 30-70% FPR contribution. Planned fix in v2.1: alias pre-pass via `ast.Import`/`ast.ImportFrom` traversal with `__init__.py` chain resolution (max 3 hops).\n\n**Severity policy**:\n- **critical**: execution/dispatch/enforcement behavior depends on the seam\n- **major**: seam is dead but local fallback exists\n- **info**: whitelisted intentional optional\n\n#### 5.2.2 Orphan Module Analysis\n\n**Purpose**: Detect Python files in provider directories whose exported functions are never imported by any consumer.\n\n**Algorithm**:\n\n```\n1. Identify provider directories by convention:\n   - names matching config.provider_dir_names\n   - directories containing 3+ Python files with common function prefix\n2. For each Python file in provider directory:\n   a. AST-parse, extract top-level def (excluding _private)\n   b. Search all Python files OUTSIDE provider dir for imports\n   c. Zero importers -> WiringFinding(orphan_module)\n```\n\n**Pattern matched**:\n```python\n# src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify/steps/validate_config.py\ndef run_validate_config():  # never imported by executor.py\n    ...\n# -> Finding: orphan_module, steps/validate_config.py::run_validate_config\n```\n\n**Exclusions**: `__init__.py`, `conftest.py`, `test_*.py`\n\n**Evidence rule**: A symbol is orphaned only if BOTH:\n1. Direct analysis finds no effective import/call chain\n2. Cleanup-audit evidence does not justify dynamic or deferred use\n\n#### 5.2.3 Unwired Registry Analysis\n\n**Purpose**: Detect dispatch registry dictionaries whose values reference non-importable functions.\n\n**Algorithm**:\n\n```\n1. AST-parse all Python files\n2. For each module-level assignment where:\n   a. Target name matches REGISTRY_PATTERNS\n   b. Value is a Dict literal\n3. For each dict entry:\n   a. If value is Name node: verify importable in scope\n   b. If value is string: verify resolves to module.function\n   c. If value is None: flag as explicit null handler\n4. Unresolvable -> WiringFinding(unwired_registry)\n```\n\n**Registry patterns** (configurable):\n```python\nDEFAULT_REGISTRY_PATTERNS = re.compile(\n    r\"^(STEP_REGISTRY|STEP_DISPATCH|PROGRAMMATIC_RUNNERS|\"\n    r\"\\w*_REGISTRY|\\w*_DISPATCH|\\w*_HANDLERS|\\w*_ROUTER|\\w*_BUILDERS)$\"\n)\n```\n\nThree detection classes:\n1. **entry unresolved** -- mapped target does not resolve -> critical\n2. **registry unused** -- registry or accessor has zero external consumers -> major\n3. **explicit None** -- entry maps to None with no alternate handler -> major\n\n### 5.3 ToolOrchestrator AST Analyzer Plugin\n\n```python\n# src/superclaude/cli/audit/wiring_analyzer.py\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport ast\nfrom pathlib import Path\n\nfrom .tool_orchestrator import FileAnalysis\n\n\ndef ast_analyze_file(file_path: Path, content: str) -> FileAnalysis:\n    \"\"\"AST-based file analyzer for ToolOrchestrator injection.\n\n    Populates the `references` field that the default line-based\n    analyzer leaves empty.\n\n    Usage: ToolOrchestrator(analyzer=ast_analyze_file)\n    \"\"\"\n    try:\n        tree = ast.parse(content, filename=str(file_path))\n    except SyntaxError:\n        return FileAnalysis(\n            imports=[], exports=[], references=[], metadata={}\n        )\n\n    imports = _extract_imports(tree)\n    exports = _extract_exports(tree)\n    references = _extract_references(tree, file_path)\n\n    return FileAnalysis(\n        imports=imports,\n        exports=exports,\n        references=references,\n        metadata={\n            \"has_dispatch_registry\": _has_registry(tree),\n            \"injectable_callables\": _count_injectable_callables(tree),\n        },\n    )\n```\n\n**Integration**: Pass as `analyzer` parameter to `ToolOrchestrator.__init__()`. This populates the empty `references` field, improving:\n- `dependency_graph.py` Tier-A edges (actual imports vs line-based)\n- `dead_code.py` detection (symbol-level vs file-level)\n- `profile_generator.py` coupling metric (real deps vs stem-matching)\n\n<!-- Source: Debate risk #2 / Refactor W-002 — ToolOrchestrator cut criteria -->\n#### 5.3.1 Cut Criteria\n\nIf T06 (ToolOrchestrator AST plugin) is not complete by the time T08 (roadmap integration) begins, defer T06 to v2.1. Core wiring gate functionality (T01-T05, T07-T10) does not depend on the ToolOrchestrator plugin. The cleanup-audit integration (Mode C) operates with reduced accuracy but still functions using line-based analysis.\n\n### 5.4 Report Format\n\nYAML frontmatter + Markdown body, conforming to `GateCriteria` validation:\n\n```yaml\n---\ngate: wiring-verification\ntarget_dir: src/superclaude/cli/cli_portify\nfiles_analyzed: 14\nfiles_skipped: 0\nrollout_mode: shadow\nanalysis_complete: true\naudit_artifacts_used: 0\nunwired_callable_count: 1\norphan_module_count: 2\nunwired_registry_count: 0\ncritical_count: 3\nmajor_count: 0\ninfo_count: 0\ntotal_findings: 3\nblocking_findings: 3\nwhitelist_entries_applied: 0\n---\n```\n\n<!-- Source: Invariant INV-014 — flat frontmatter confirmed, no nested severity_summary block -->\n\n**Serialization**: All string-valued frontmatter fields MUST use `yaml.safe_dump()` to prevent YAML injection. Integer/boolean gate-evaluated fields are exempt.\n\n**Whitelist visibility**: `whitelist_entries_applied` is ALWAYS present. Zero if no whitelist configured.\n\n<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 7.3 — required report body sections (S-002) -->\n#### 5.4.1 Required Body Sections\n\nThe Markdown body of the wiring verification report MUST contain these 7 sections in order:\n\n1. **Summary** -- overall finding counts, scope analyzed, rollout mode\n2. **Unwired Optional Callable Injections** -- per-finding detail for `unwired_callable` type\n3. **Orphan Modules / Symbols** -- per-finding detail for `orphan_module` type\n4. **Unregistered Dispatch Entries** -- per-finding detail for `unwired_registry` type\n5. **Suppressions and Dynamic Retention** -- whitelist entries applied, audit evidence used\n6. **Recommended Remediation** -- actionable fix guidance per finding category\n7. **Evidence and Limitations** -- known FPR sources, alias limitations, analysis boundaries\n\nThis ensures human-readable reports have consistent structure across runs and are useful for both automated gate validation and manual review.\n\n<!-- Source: Invariant INV-001 / Refactor W-004 — _extract_frontmatter_values() helper -->\n### 5.5 Frontmatter Value Extraction\n\nAll semantic check functions share a private helper:\n\n```python\ndef _extract_frontmatter_values(content: str) -> dict[str, str]:\n    \"\"\"Extract frontmatter key-value pairs from report content.\n\n    Uses the _FRONTMATTER_RE regex pattern (duplicated from\n    pipeline/gates.py:77 as a private constant to preserve\n    NFR-007 layering) to extract frontmatter key-value pairs.\n\n    Returns a dict mapping each key to its raw string value.\n    Each semantic check calls this helper once and casts values\n    as needed (int(), string comparison).\n    \"\"\"\n```\n\nThis helper lives in `audit/wiring_gate.py`, not in `pipeline/*`, preserving the layering constraint (NFR-007). Estimated: ~15 LOC.\n\n**Why not modify `_check_frontmatter()`**: That function is in `pipeline/gates.py` which must remain domain-agnostic. Adding a value-extraction return type would change its contract, violating the \"zero changes to pipeline/*\" constraint.\n\n### 5.6 Gate Definition\n\n```python\nWIRING_GATE = GateCriteria(\n    required_frontmatter_fields=[\n        \"gate\",\n        \"target_dir\",\n        \"files_analyzed\",\n        \"rollout_mode\",\n        \"analysis_complete\",\n        \"unwired_callable_count\",\n        \"orphan_module_count\",\n        \"unwired_registry_count\",\n        \"critical_count\",\n        \"major_count\",\n        \"info_count\",\n        \"total_findings\",\n        \"blocking_findings\",\n        \"whitelist_entries_applied\",\n        \"files_skipped\",\n        \"audit_artifacts_used\",\n    ],\n    min_lines=10,\n    enforcement_tier=\"STRICT\",\n    semantic_checks=[\n        SemanticCheck(\n            name=\"analysis_complete_true\",\n            check_fn=_analysis_complete_true,\n            failure_message=\"analysis_complete must be true\",\n        ),\n        SemanticCheck(\n            name=\"recognized_rollout_mode\",\n            check_fn=_recognized_rollout_mode,\n            failure_message=\"rollout_mode must be shadow, soft, or full\",\n        ),\n        SemanticCheck(\n            name=\"finding_counts_consistent\",\n            check_fn=_finding_counts_consistent,\n            failure_message=(\n                \"total_findings must equal \"\n                \"unwired_callable_count + orphan_module_count + unwired_registry_count\"\n            ),\n        ),\n        SemanticCheck(\n            name=\"severity_summary_consistent\",\n            check_fn=_severity_summary_consistent,\n            failure_message=(\n                \"critical_count + major_count + info_count must equal total_findings\"\n            ),\n        ),\n        SemanticCheck(\n            name=\"zero_blocking_findings_for_mode\",\n            check_fn=_zero_blocking_findings_for_mode,\n            failure_message=\"blocking_findings must be 0 for gate pass at current rollout_mode\",\n        ),\n    ],\n)\n```\n\n**Mode-aware enforcement** (key design decision):\n\nThe `_zero_blocking_findings_for_mode` check reads `rollout_mode` and `blocking_findings` from frontmatter:\n- **shadow**: always returns `True` (findings logged, never block)\n- **soft**: returns `True` if `blocking_findings == 0` (only critical block)\n- **full**: returns `True` if `blocking_findings == 0` (all findings block)\n\nThe `blocking_findings` field is computed by the emitter based on rollout mode:\n- shadow: `blocking_findings = 0` always\n- soft: `blocking_findings = critical_count`\n- full: `blocking_findings = critical_count + major_count`\n\nThis encodes rollout policy into the report artifact, keeping semantic checks as pure content validators per the `SemanticCheck` contract.\n\n### 5.7 Roadmap Pipeline Integration\n\n**5-step process** (per gate-system-deep-analysis Section 8):\n\n**Step 1**: Define `WIRING_GATE` in `audit/wiring_gate.py`\n\n**Step 2**: Define prompt in `roadmap/prompts.py`:\n```python\ndef build_wiring_verification_prompt(merge_file: Path, spec_source: str) -> str:\n    \"\"\"Prompt for wiring-verification step (deterministic, not LLM).\"\"\"\n    return \"\"  # Non-LLM step; prompt unused but required by Step contract\n```\n\n**Step 3**: Import into `roadmap/executor.py`\n\n**Step 4**: Add to `_build_steps()` after `spec-fidelity` (line 473):\n```python\nStep(\n    id=\"wiring-verification\",\n    prompt=build_wiring_verification_prompt(merge_file, spec_source),\n    output_file=out / \"wiring-verification.md\",\n    gate=WIRING_GATE,\n    timeout_seconds=60,\n    inputs=[merge_file, spec_fidelity_file],\n    retry_limit=0,                         # Deterministic; retry won't help\n    gate_mode=GateMode.TRAILING,           # Shadow: non-blocking\n),\n```\n\n<!-- Source: Invariant INV-012 — retry_limit=0 semantics documented -->\n**`retry_limit=0` semantics**: Per `pipeline/executor.py:158`, `max_attempts = retry_limit + 1`. So `retry_limit=0` means the step executes exactly once with no retries. This is correct for a deterministic step where re-execution produces identical results. The only retry-worthy scenario (transient filesystem errors) should be handled within the analysis function itself.\n\n<!-- Source: Invariant INV-003 — explicit _get_all_step_ids() synchronization requirement -->\n**Step 5**: Update `_get_all_step_ids()` (line 538) and `ALL_GATES` (line 933).\n\n`_get_all_step_ids()` MUST be updated to include `\"wiring-verification\"` after `\"spec-fidelity\"` and before `\"remediate\"`. The existing desynchronization between `_build_steps()` (8 steps) and `_get_all_step_ids()` (11 IDs including `remediate` and `certify`) is intentional -- `remediate` and `certify` are conditionally executed steps. `wiring-verification` belongs in the unconditional pipeline, so it goes in both functions.\n\n<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 5.3 — why _build_steps() is the correct insertion point (S-001) -->\n#### 5.7.1 Why `_build_steps()` Is the Correct Insertion Point\n\nThe codebase has no dynamic gate registry for roadmap execution. Gates are wired statically at `Step` construction time. The integration point is not an external registry; it is a new `Step(...)` entry in `_build_steps()`.\n\nThe repository already contains a design precedent for a post-merge deterministic step: the anti-instinct audit step is modeled as a normal `Step` in `_build_steps()` but handled specially by the executor as a non-LLM operation. That is the correct pattern for wiring verification as well.\n\n**Executor special-casing**: In `roadmap_run_step()`, detect `step.id == \"wiring-verification\"`:\n```python\nif step.id == \"wiring-verification\":\n    report = run_wiring_analysis(target_dir=config.source_dir)\n    emit_report(report, step.output_file, enforcement_mode=config.wiring_rollout_mode)\n    return StepResult(step=step, status=StepStatus.PASS)\n```\n\n**Shadow**: `GateMode.TRAILING` uses `TrailingGateRunner` for async non-blocking evaluation. Failures persist to `DeferredRemediationLog`.\n\n**Full**: Switch to `GateMode.BLOCKING`. `resolve_gate_mode()` forces release scope to BLOCKING regardless.\n\n<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 9.3 — resume behavior (S-003) -->\n#### 5.7.2 Resume Behavior\n\nBecause the roadmap pipeline already resumes by gate-passing existing artifacts, the new wiring-verification step naturally fits current resume behavior if:\n\n1. `wiring-verification.md` is deterministic (same inputs produce same output)\n2. Its gate result is reproducible (semantic checks are pure functions over content)\n3. `_get_all_step_ids()` is updated to include `wiring-verification`\n\nNo special resume handling is required. The existing resume mechanism detects the output file, evaluates the gate, and skips the step if the gate passes.\n\n### 5.8 Sprint Integration\n\n```python\n# sprint/models.py\nwiring_gate_mode: Literal[\"off\", \"shadow\", \"soft\", \"full\"] = \"shadow\"\n\n# sprint/executor.py -- after task classification\nif config.wiring_gate_mode != \"off\":\n    wiring_report_path = work_dir / f\"{task_id}-wiring-report.md\"\n    report = run_wiring_analysis(target_dir=config.source_dir)\n    emit_report(report, wiring_report_path,\n                enforcement_mode=config.wiring_gate_mode)\n\n    if config.wiring_gate_mode == \"shadow\":\n        logger.info(f\"[shadow] Wiring gate: {report.total_findings} findings\")\n    elif config.wiring_gate_mode == \"soft\":\n        if not report.clean:\n            tui.warn(f\"Wiring gate: {report.total_findings} findings\")\n    elif config.wiring_gate_mode == \"full\":\n        passed, reason = gate_passed(wiring_report_path, WIRING_GATE)\n        if not passed:\n            ...  # Trigger SprintGatePolicy.build_remediation_step()\n```\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n## 6. Cleanup-Audit Agent Integration\n\n### 6.1 Agent Extension Summary\n\nAll 5 agents are behavioral specs (`.md` files in `src/superclaude/agents/`). Extensions are additive -- no tools change, no existing rules removed.\n\n| Agent | Tools | Change |\n|-------|-------|--------|\n| audit-scanner (Haiku) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add `REVIEW:wiring` classification signal |\n| audit-analyzer (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add 9th mandatory field: \"Wiring path\" |\n| audit-comparator (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add cross-file wiring consistency check |\n| audit-validator (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob | Add Check 5: Wiring Claim Verification |\n| audit-consolidator (Sonnet) | Read, Grep, Glob, Write | Add \"Wiring Health\" section to report |\n\n### 6.2 audit-scanner: REVIEW:wiring Signal\n\nFor Python source files, check:\n- File contains `Optional[Callable]` parameter with `= None` default\n- File defines module-level dict matching `*_REGISTRY`, `*_DISPATCH`, `*_HANDLERS`\n- File is in a provider directory (`steps/`, `handlers/`, `validators/`, `checks/`)\n\nFiles with wiring indicators get `REVIEW:wiring`, proceeding to Pass 2 even if otherwise `KEEP`.\n\n### 6.3 audit-analyzer: 9th Mandatory Field\n\nFor `REVIEW:wiring` files, add:\n\n| Field | Description |\n|-------|-------------|\n| Wiring path | Declaration -> Registration -> Invocation chain. Each link stated or \"MISSING\" |\n\nNew finding types:\n- `UNWIRED_DECLARATION` -- symbol declared but never registered/invoked\n- `BROKEN_REGISTRATION` -- registry entry references non-importable function\n\n### 6.4 audit-validator: Check 5\n\n**Wiring Claim Verification**:\n1. Verify declared callable parameters against call site arguments\n2. Verify registry entries resolve to importable symbols\n3. Verify \"Wiring path\" field chain is complete\n\n**Critical fail**: DELETE recommendation on a file with a live wiring path.\n\n### 6.5 ToolOrchestrator Integration\n\n```python\norchestrator = ToolOrchestrator(analyzer=ast_analyze_file)\n```\n\nPopulates `FileAnalysis.references`, improving `dependency_graph.py`, `dead_code.py`, `profile_generator.py`.\n\n### 6.6 Authority Rule\n\n**Hybrid mode**: Direct deterministic analysis is authoritative. Cleanup-audit evidence acts as false-positive suppressor. Correctness does not depend on prior audit runs.\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original), with incorporations from Variant C (S-005, FPR calibration) and Invariant INV-006 (W-003, grace_period) -->\n## 7. Rollout Plan\n\n### Phase 1: Shadow (this release)\n\n**Pre-activation checklist** (blocking):\n1. Confirm `provider_dir_names` matches at least one real directory\n2. First-run zero-findings sanity check (>50 files must produce >0 findings)\n\n**Behavior**: Roadmap `GateMode.TRAILING` + Sprint `shadow` + Cleanup-audit `REVIEW:wiring`\n\n<!-- Source: Invariant INV-006 / Refactor W-003 — grace_period interaction note -->\n**Operational note on `grace_period` interaction**: Roadmap configurations should set `grace_period > 0` during shadow rollout to enable `GateMode.TRAILING` behavior via `TrailingGateRunner`. If `grace_period = 0` forces BLOCKING (per `pipeline/executor.py:160-163`), shadow mode still passes because `_zero_blocking_findings_for_mode` reads `rollout_mode=shadow` from frontmatter and returns True unconditionally, and the emitter sets `blocking_findings=0` in shadow mode. However, TRAILING mode provides cleaner operational semantics (deferred evaluation rather than immediate pass-through).\n\n### Phase 2: Soft (release +1)\n\n**Criteria**: FPR < 15%, TPR > 50%, p95 < 5s\n\n<!-- Source: Variant C, Section 9 Phase 2 — FPR calibration formula (S-005) -->\n**FPR calibration**: Set thresholds at `measured_FPR + 2 sigma` above re-export noise floor. Phase 2 MUST NOT activate if unwired-callable FPR cannot be separated from noise. This statistical approach prevents premature soft-mode activation when FPR variance is high.\n\n**Behavior**: `rollout_mode=soft`, `blocking_findings = critical_count`\n\n### Phase 3: Full (release +2)\n\n**Criteria**: FPR < 5%, TPR > 80%, whitelist stable 5+ sprints\n\n**Behavior**: `GateMode.BLOCKING`, `rollout_mode=full`, `blocking_findings = critical + major`\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n## 8. Interface Contracts\n\n### 8.1 Public API\n\n```python\ndef run_wiring_analysis(target_dir: Path, config: WiringConfig | None = None) -> WiringReport\ndef emit_report(report: WiringReport, output_path: Path, enforcement_mode: str = \"shadow\") -> None\ndef ast_analyze_file(file_path: Path, content: str) -> FileAnalysis\n```\n\n### 8.2 Gate Contract\n\n| Frontmatter Field | Type | Pass Condition |\n|-------------------|------|----------------|\n| `gate` | string | `\"wiring-verification\"` |\n| `target_dir` | string | Non-empty |\n| `files_analyzed` | int | >= 0 |\n| `files_skipped` | int | >= 0 |\n| `rollout_mode` | string | `shadow` / `soft` / `full` |\n| `analysis_complete` | bool | `true` |\n| `unwired_callable_count` | int | Present |\n| `orphan_module_count` | int | Present |\n| `unwired_registry_count` | int | Present |\n| `critical_count` | int | Present |\n| `major_count` | int | Present |\n| `info_count` | int | Present |\n| `total_findings` | int | = sum of type counts |\n| `blocking_findings` | int | Must be 0 |\n| `whitelist_entries_applied` | int | >= 0 |\n\n### 8.3 Dependency Direction\n\n```\naudit/wiring_gate.py    --> pipeline/models.py     (GateCriteria, SemanticCheck)\naudit/wiring_analyzer.py --> audit/tool_orchestrator.py (FileAnalysis)\naudit/wiring_config.py  --> (stdlib only)\nroadmap/executor.py     --> audit/wiring_gate.py\nsprint/executor.py      --> audit/wiring_gate.py\npipeline/*              --> NOTHING from audit/roadmap/sprint\n```\n\n---\n\n<!-- Source: Base (original) -->\n## 9. Decisions\n\n| # | Decision | Rationale |\n|---|----------|-----------|\n| D1 | Enforcement is artifact-based | Fits SemanticCheck contract: `check_fn(content: str) -> bool` validates report content, not repository state |\n| D2 | Deterministic Python, not LLM | Wiring needs precision; LLM synthesis rejected as \"too weak for wiring assurance and too dependent on narrative interpretation\" (see D2a below) |\n| D3 | Extend audit-analyzer, no new agent | Reuse 8-field profile; single \"Wiring path\" chain field forces full chain tracing |\n| D4 | Insert via _build_steps() after spec-fidelity | Static wiring pattern; no dynamic gate registry exists (see Section 5.7.1) |\n| D5 | Shadow/soft/full via rollout_mode frontmatter | No parallel infra; policy encoded in artifact, checks remain pure content validators |\n| D6 | GateMode.TRAILING for shadow phase | Existing TrailingGateRunner; mode-aware checks as safeguard if BLOCKING forced |\n| D7 | AST analyzer as ToolOrchestrator plugin | Reuses existing seam; parallel track with explicit cut criteria |\n\n<!-- Source: Variant A, Section 9.1 — rejected option documentation (S-008) -->\n### D2a: Rejected Alternative -- LLM Report Generation\n\n**Rejected**: LLM-only report generation from pre-read analyses.\n\n**Reason**: Too weak for wiring assurance and too dependent on narrative interpretation. Wiring verification requires deterministic precision (exact symbol resolution, exact import chain tracing) that LLM synthesis cannot reliably provide. Your job is to quickly classify files as DELETE, REVIEW, or KEEP based on evidence from reading file content and grepping for references.\n\n## Safety Constraint\n**DO NOT modify, edit, delete, move, or rename ANY existing file. Violation = task failure.** You may only write your output report.\n\n## Input\nYou will receive:\n1. A list of files to audit (your batch)\n2. The batch number and total batch count\n3. The output file path for your report\n\n## Methodology\n\nFor each file in your batch:\n\n1. **Read** first 20-30 lines to understand purpose and identify file type\n2. **Grep** for the filename across the repo: `grep -r \"filename\" --exclude-dir=.git --exclude-dir=node_modules`\n3. **Check imports**: Verify file is not imported/sourced by other files (check import/require/source statements, package.json, Makefile, CI workflows)\n4. **Categorize** as DELETE/REVIEW/KEEP with brief justification\n\n## Classification Taxonomy\n\n| Category | Criteria | Evidence Required |\n|----------|----------|-------------------|\n| **DELETE** | Zero references, no value, clearly obsolete | Grep proof: pattern + count + zero-result |\n| **REVIEW** | Uncertain — may be needed, needs human judgment | Brief justification of uncertainty |\n| **KEEP** | Actively referenced, part of build/runtime/CI | At least one reference cited (file:line) |\n\n## Conservative Bias\n- When uncertain, classify as **REVIEW**, never DELETE\n- A file named `old-deploy.sh` might be the only deploy script that works — read it first\n- \"No imports found\" without grep evidence is NOT sufficient for DELETE\n\n## Dynamic Loading Check\nBefore classifying any file as DELETE, verify it is not dynamically loaded:\n- Environment variable-based module loading\n- String-based import loaders (template literals, f-strings)\n- Plugin registries\n- Glob-based file discovery\n- Config-driven loading patterns\n\nIf any pattern could load the file, classify as REVIEW.\n\n## Binary Asset Handling\nFor binary files (images, fonts, videos): grep-only audit (reference checking without reading content). KEEP if referenced, REVIEW if unreferenced but in expected asset directory, DELETE only if in unexpected location AND zero references.\n\n## Output Format\n\nWrite your report following this structure:\n\n```markdown\n# {Scope} Audit (Pass 1)\n\n**Status**: Complete\n**Files audited**: X / Y assigned\n**Date**: YYYY-MM-DD\n\n## Safe to Delete\n- [ ] `filepath` — reason (grep: 0 references, pattern: \"filename\")\n\n## Need Decision\n- [ ] `filepath` — what it is, why uncertain\n\n## Keep (verified legitimate)\n- `filepath` — why needed (referenced by: file:line)\n\n## Add to .gitignore\n- `pattern` — reason\n\n## Remaining / Not Audited\n- (list any files not reached)\n\n## Summary\n- DELETE: N | REVIEW: N | KEEP: N | .gitignore: N\n```\n\n## Incremental Save Protocol\n1. profiles), perform cross-referential integrity checks to detect wiring inconsistencies that per-file analysis misses.\n\n### Consistency Checks\n\n1. **Orphan Claims**: File A's Wiring path claims it wires callable X, but file X's profile shows no inbound wiring consumer → flag as `ORPHAN_WIRING_CLAIM`\n2. **Phantom Consumers**: File B's Wiring path claims to consume callable from file C, but file C does not export that callable or does not exist → flag as `PHANTOM_CONSUMER`\n3. **Registry Cross-Reference**: If file A defines a registry and file B is listed as a registry target, verify file B's profile confirms it is registered → flag mismatches as `REGISTRY_MISMATCH`\n4. **Bidirectional Verification**: For every wiring claim in file A referencing file B, check that file B's profile acknowledges file A as a consumer or provider\n\n### Wiring Inconsistency Types\n\n| Type | Evidence Required | Severity |\n|------|-------------------|----------|\n| **ORPHAN_WIRING_CLAIM** | File A claims wiring to B, but B shows no corresponding link | Major |\n| **PHANTOM_CONSUMER** | File references a provider that does not exist or does not export the claimed symbol | Critical |\n| **REGISTRY_MISMATCH** | Registry entry and target file disagree on registration status | Major |\n\n### Output Addition\n\nAdd a **Wiring Consistency Matrix** section to the report when wiring-flagged You must quantify overlap and produce duplication matrices.\n\n## Safety Constraint\n**DO NOT modify, edit, delete, move, or rename ANY existing file. Evidence required |\n| **Currently used?** | Referenced by running app, CI/CD, build? Cite specific references |\n| **Recommendation** | DELETE / CONSOLIDATE (with what) / MOVE / FLAG / KEEP — reason |\n\n## 6 Critical Differentiators\n\n1. **Compare, don't just catalog**: When similar files found, DIFF them. State \"X and Y are N% identical, differing in sections A, B\"\n2. **Group audit**: Audit similar files together.
